THE

KALATATTVAVIVECHANA

BY

RAGHUNATHA BHAс╣мс╣мA

With a Foreword by

PRINCIPAL GOPINATH KAVIRAJ

Edited with Introduction, Notes, etc.

By

NANDA KISHORE SHARMA

S─Бhity─Бch─Бrya, Ved─Бntabh┼лshana. Research Scholar,
Government Sanskrit Library,
BENARES.

1932.

FOREWORD.

тАФтАФтАФтАФтАФ

Thanks to the enterprise of industrious scholars and of the patrons of ancient Sanskrit Learning, the important works of Sanskrit literature are being slowly reclaimed from oblivion and placed before the public. In Dharma ┼Ъ─Бstra, however, as in some other branches, there remains yet a huge mass of literary material waiting for the editorial adventure of the skilled workman and for publication. The work presented in the following pages represents an important piece of literary composition in the field of Dharma ┼Ъ─Бstra and has a position of its own in its history.
The K─Бlatattva Vivechana of Raghun─Бtha Bhaс╣нс╣нa, known under the designation of Samr─Бt Sthapati, deals with all the important questions relating to the observance of tithi, etc. The relative value of this work can be determined by a reference, by way of comparison, to other works of a similar nature belonging to the same or to the rival schools. But there appears to be no doubt, as a cursory glance through the pages will suffice to show, that for a student of Dharma ┼Ъ─Бstra from a comparative standpoint a careful study of the book is sure to yield interesting results.
The author was the second son of M─Бdhava Bhaс╣нс╣нa, the youngest brother of the famous N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa Bhaс╣нс╣нa, who was one of the most learned authors at Benares in the 16th century. N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa was the author of Dharma pravс╣Ыitti, Prayoga ratna, etc. and was a contemporary of the great philosopher Madhu S┼лdana Sarasvat─л with whom he often took part in literary polemics. Raghun─Бtha had an elder brother named Vi┼Ыvan─Бtha and a younger one whose name was Prabh─Бkara and whose most promising career was cut short by an untimely death. It was this Prabh─Бkara Bhaс╣нс╣нa who wrote the Rasaprad─лpa (published in this Series as No. 12) in the year 1593 A. D. The K─Бlatattva Vivechana was composed in Samvat 1677 (= 1620 A.D.). The author describes himself as well versed in Dharma ┼Ъ─Бstra and M─лm─Бms─Б(рдореАрдорд╛рдВрд╕рд╛рдзрд░реНрдорд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗрд╖реБ рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреНрдХреГрддрдкрд░рд┐рд╢реНрд░рдордГ) and is credited with the composition of several treatises on these subjects. It may be noted here for general information that R─Бma Chandra Bhaс╣нс╣нa Tatsat, the well known author of Krityaratn─Бval─л(written in 1648 A.D.) and K─Бlanirс╣Зayaprak─Б┼Ыa was the daughter’s son of Raghun─Бtha. The present edition of the work undertaken by one of the Sadholal Research Scholars of the Sanskrit College, is based on a single manuscript belonging to the Library of the College bearing Samvat 1745 (= 1688 A.D.) as the date of its transcription.
A detailed study of the work and its author, both historically and critically on the basis of its contents, will follow shortly in the Introduction in the second part.

Government Sanskrit College,
GOPINATHA KAVIRAJ.
BENARES.

“рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдВ рди рднреБрдЮреНрдЬреАрдд рдкрдХреНрд╖рдпреЛрд░реБрднрдпреЛрд░рдкрд┐ред

“рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢реНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛ рд░рдгреНрдбрд╛ рдпрддрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕реБрдорд╣рд╛рдорддреЗред

(f) History and Bibliography of Nyaya Vaisesika Literature, by Gopinath Kaviraj.

Vol. VIIтАФ

(j) Descriptive notes on Sanskrit Manuscripts, by Gopinatha Kaviraj.
